	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">House of Windsor</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="fn org" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold">House of Windsor</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:Badge_of_the_House_of_Windsor.svg" class="image"><img alt="Badge of the House of Windsor.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Badge_of_the_House_of_Windsor.svg/140px-Badge_of_the_House_of_Windsor.svg.png" decoding="async" width="140" height="177" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Badge_of_the_House_of_Windsor.svg/210px-Badge_of_the_House_of_Windsor.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Badge_of_the_House_of_Windsor.svg/280px-Badge_of_the_House_of_Windsor.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="563" data-file-height="710" /></a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Parent house</th><td><a href="/wiki/House_of_Wettin" title="House of Wettin">Wettin</a> → <a href="/wiki/House_of_Saxe-Coburg_and_Gotha" title="House of Saxe-Coburg and Gotha">Saxe-Coburg and Gotha</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Country</th><td class="label"><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> and the other <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realms</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Founded</th><td>17&#160;July 1917<span class="noprint">&#59;&#32;102 years ago</span><span style="display:none">&#160;(<span class="bday dtstart published updated">1917-07-17</span>)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Founder</th><td><a href="/wiki/George_V" title="George V">George V</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Current head</th><td><a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>House of Windsor</b> is the reigning <a href="/wiki/Royal_house" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal house">royal house</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> and the other <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realms</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Dynasty" title="Dynasty">dynasty</a> is originally of <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">German</a> paternal descent and was a branch of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Saxe-Coburg_and_Gotha" title="House of Saxe-Coburg and Gotha">House of Saxe-Coburg and Gotha</a>, itself derived from the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Wettin" title="House of Wettin">House of Wettin</a>, which succeeded the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hanover" title="House of Hanover">House of Hanover</a> to the <a href="/wiki/British_monarchy" class="mw-redirect" title="British monarchy">British monarchy</a> following the death of <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a>, wife of <a href="/wiki/Albert,_Prince_Consort" title="Albert, Prince Consort">Albert, Prince Consort</a>.
</p><p>The name was changed from <i>Saxe-Coburg and Gotha</i> to the English <i>Windsor</i> (from <a href="/wiki/Windsor_Castle" title="Windsor Castle">Windsor Castle</a><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>) in 1917 because of <a href="/wiki/Anti-German_sentiment" title="Anti-German sentiment">anti-German sentiment</a> in the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-jim2001_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jim2001-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> There have been four British monarchs of the house of Windsor to date: three kings and the present queen, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a>. During the reign of the Windsors, there have been major changes in British society. The British Empire participated in the First and <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World Wars</a>, ending up on the winning side both times, but subsequently lost its status as a <a href="/wiki/Superpower" title="Superpower">superpower</a> during <a href="/wiki/Decolonisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Decolonisation">decolonisation</a>. Much of Ireland broke with the United Kingdom and the remnants of the Empire became the <a href="/wiki/British_Commonwealth" class="mw-redirect" title="British Commonwealth">British Commonwealth</a> and, subsequently, the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>.
</p><p>The current head of the house is monarch of sixteen <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign states</a>. These are the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> (where they are based), <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">the Bahamas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Saint Kitts and Nevis">Saint Kitts and Nevis</a>. As well as these separate monarchies, there are also three <a href="/wiki/Crown_dependencies" title="Crown dependencies">Crown dependencies</a>, fourteen <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territories</a> and two <a href="/wiki/Associated_state" title="Associated state">associated states</a> of New Zealand.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Windsor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_Good_Riddance_-_George_V_of_the_United_Kingdom_cartoon_in_Punch,_1917.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/A_Good_Riddance_-_George_V_of_the_United_Kingdom_cartoon_in_Punch%2C_1917.png/220px-A_Good_Riddance_-_George_V_of_the_United_Kingdom_cartoon_in_Punch%2C_1917.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="282" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/A_Good_Riddance_-_George_V_of_the_United_Kingdom_cartoon_in_Punch%2C_1917.png/330px-A_Good_Riddance_-_George_V_of_the_United_Kingdom_cartoon_in_Punch%2C_1917.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/A_Good_Riddance_-_George_V_of_the_United_Kingdom_cartoon_in_Punch%2C_1917.png/440px-A_Good_Riddance_-_George_V_of_the_United_Kingdom_cartoon_in_Punch%2C_1917.png 2x" data-file-width="1356" data-file-height="1736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_Good_Riddance_-_George_V_of_the_United_Kingdom_cartoon_in_Punch,_1917.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"A Good Riddance"; cartoon from <i><a href="/wiki/Punch_(magazine)" title="Punch (magazine)">Punch</a></i>, Vol. 152, 27 June 1917, commenting on the King's order to relinquish all German titles held by members of his family</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Edward_VII" title="Edward VII">Edward VII</a> and, in turn, his son, <a href="/wiki/George_V" title="George V">George V</a>, were members of the German <a href="/wiki/Ducal" class="mw-redirect" title="Ducal">ducal</a> <a href="/wiki/House_of_Saxe-Coburg_and_Gotha" title="House of Saxe-Coburg and Gotha">House of Saxe-Coburg and Gotha</a> by virtue of their descent from <a href="/wiki/Albert,_Prince_Consort" title="Albert, Prince Consort">Albert, Prince Consort</a>, husband of <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a>, the last British monarch from the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hanover" title="House of Hanover">House of Hanover</a>. High <a href="/wiki/Anti-German_sentiment" title="Anti-German sentiment">anti-German sentiment</a> amongst the people of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> during World War I reached a peak in March 1917, when the <a href="/wiki/Gotha_G.IV" title="Gotha G.IV">Gotha G.IV</a>, a heavy aircraft capable of crossing the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a>, began bombing London directly and became a household name. In the same year, on 15 March, King George's first cousin, <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_II_of_Russia" title="Nicholas II of Russia">Nicholas II</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Emperor of Russia">Emperor of Russia</a>, was forced to <a href="/wiki/Abdication" title="Abdication">abdicate</a>, which raised the spectre of the eventual abolition of all the monarchies in Europe. The King and his family were finally convinced to abandon all titles held under the German Crown and to change German titles and house names to anglicised versions. Hence, on 17 July 1917, a <a href="/wiki/Royal_proclamation" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal proclamation">royal proclamation</a> issued by George V declared:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Now, therefore, We, out of Our Royal Will and Authority, do hereby declare and announce that as from the date of this Our Royal Proclamation Our House and Family shall be styled and known as the House and Family of Windsor, and that all the descendants in the male line of Our said Grandmother Queen Victoria who are subjects of these Realms, other than female descendants who may marry or may have married, shall bear the said Name of Windsor....<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>The name had a long association with monarchy in Britain, through the town of <a href="/wiki/Windsor,_Berkshire" title="Windsor, Berkshire">Windsor, Berkshire</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Windsor_Castle" title="Windsor Castle">Windsor Castle</a>; the link is alluded to in the Round Tower of Windsor Castle being the basis of the badge of the House of Windsor. Upon hearing that his cousin had changed the name of the British royal house to Windsor and in reference to <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">Shakespeare</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Merry_Wives_of_Windsor" title="The Merry Wives of Windsor">The Merry Wives of Windsor</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_German_monarchs" title="List of German monarchs">German Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_II,_German_Emperor" title="Wilhelm II, German Emperor">Wilhelm II</a> remarked jokingly that he planned to see "The Merry Wives of Saxe-Coburg-Gotha".<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>George V also restricted the use of <a href="/wiki/British_prince" title="British prince">British princely</a> titles to his nearest relations,<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and in 1919, he stripped three of his German relations of their British titles and styles.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Members">Members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Windsor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_British_royal_family_on_the_balcony_of_Buckingham_Palace.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/The_British_royal_family_on_the_balcony_of_Buckingham_Palace.JPG/220px-The_British_royal_family_on_the_balcony_of_Buckingham_Palace.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/The_British_royal_family_on_the_balcony_of_Buckingham_Palace.JPG/330px-The_British_royal_family_on_the_balcony_of_Buckingham_Palace.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/The_British_royal_family_on_the_balcony_of_Buckingham_Palace.JPG/440px-The_British_royal_family_on_the_balcony_of_Buckingham_Palace.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_British_royal_family_on_the_balcony_of_Buckingham_Palace.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Members of the House of Windsor on the balcony of Buckingham Palace, 15 June 2013. Left to right: <a href="/wiki/Prince_Richard,_Duke_of_Gloucester" title="Prince Richard, Duke of Gloucester">Prince Richard, Duke of Gloucester</a>; <a href="/wiki/Lady_Rose_Gilman" class="mw-redirect" title="Lady Rose Gilman">Lady Rose Gilman</a>; <a href="/wiki/Prince_Michael_of_Kent" title="Prince Michael of Kent">Prince Michael of Kent</a>; <a href="/wiki/Princess_Michael_of_Kent" title="Princess Michael of Kent">Princess Michael of Kent</a>; <a href="/wiki/Lady_Louise_Windsor" title="Lady Louise Windsor">Lady Louise Windsor</a>; <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward,_Earl_of_Wessex" title="Prince Edward, Earl of Wessex">Prince Edward, Earl of Wessex</a>; <a href="/wiki/James,_Viscount_Severn" title="James, Viscount Severn">James, Viscount Severn</a>; <a href="/wiki/Sophie,_Countess_of_Wessex" title="Sophie, Countess of Wessex">Sophie, Countess of Wessex</a>; <a href="/wiki/Camilla,_Duchess_of_Cornwall" title="Camilla, Duchess of Cornwall">Camilla, Duchess of Cornwall</a>; <a href="/wiki/Charles,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Charles, Prince of Wales">Prince Charles, Prince of Wales</a>; <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a>; <a href="/wiki/Anne,_Princess_Royal" title="Anne, Princess Royal">Princess Anne, Princess Royal</a>; <a href="/wiki/Prince_Andrew,_Duke_of_York" title="Prince Andrew, Duke of York">Prince Andrew, Duke of York</a>; <a href="/wiki/Prince_Harry,_Duke_of_Sussex" title="Prince Harry, Duke of Sussex">Prince Harry, Duke of Sussex</a>; <a href="/wiki/Catherine,_Duchess_of_Cambridge" title="Catherine, Duchess of Cambridge">Catherine, Duchess of Cambridge</a>; <a href="/wiki/Prince_William,_Duke_of_Cambridge" title="Prince William, Duke of Cambridge">Prince William, Duke of Cambridge</a>; <a href="/wiki/Princess_Eugenie_of_York" title="Princess Eugenie of York">Princess Eugenie of York</a>; <a href="/wiki/Princess_Beatrice_of_York" title="Princess Beatrice of York">Princess Beatrice of York</a>; <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward,_Duke_of_Kent" title="Prince Edward, Duke of Kent">Prince Edward, Duke of Kent</a>; <a href="/wiki/Katharine,_Duchess_of_Kent" title="Katharine, Duchess of Kent">Katharine, Duchess of Kent</a></div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_members_of_the_House_of_Windsor" title="List of members of the House of Windsor">List of members of the House of Windsor</a></div>
<p>The 1917 proclamation stated that the name of the Royal House and all British descendants of Victoria and Albert in the male line were to bear the name of Windsor, except for women who married into other families.
</p><p>By early 1919 the living male-line British descendants of Victoria subject to British rule were King George V, his five sons, his daughter <a href="/wiki/Mary,_Princess_Royal_and_Countess_of_Harewood" title="Mary, Princess Royal and Countess of Harewood">Princess Mary</a>, his unmarried sister <a href="/wiki/Princess_Victoria_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Princess Victoria of the United Kingdom">Princess Victoria</a>, his uncle <a href="/wiki/Prince_Arthur,_Duke_of_Connaught_and_Strathearn" title="Prince Arthur, Duke of Connaught and Strathearn">Prince Arthur, Duke of Connaught and Strathearn</a>, his cousin <a href="/wiki/Prince_Arthur_of_Connaught" title="Prince Arthur of Connaught">Prince Arthur of Connaught</a>, his cousin once removed <a href="/wiki/Alastair_Windsor,_2nd_Duke_of_Connaught_and_Strathearn" title="Alastair Windsor, 2nd Duke of Connaught and Strathearn">Prince Alastair of Connaught</a>, and his unmarried cousin <a href="/wiki/Princess_Patricia_of_Connaught" title="Princess Patricia of Connaught">Princess Patricia of Connaught</a>. Prince Alastair and Princess Victoria died unmarried and childless. Princess Mary married into the Lascelles family, and Princess Patricia married <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Ramsay_(Royal_Navy_officer)" title="Alexander Ramsay (Royal Navy officer)">Alexander Ramsay</a>. Neither of the Arthurs had any further children, meaning all subsequent members of the House of Windsor descend from the sons of George V.
</p><p>Two of George V's sons, <a href="/wiki/Edward_VIII" title="Edward VIII">Edward VIII</a> (later Duke of Windsor) and <a href="/wiki/Prince_John_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prince John of the United Kingdom">Prince John</a>, had no children, so the entire present day members of the House of Windsor are descendants of the other three sons: Prince Albert, Duke of York (later <a href="/wiki/George_VI" title="George VI">George VI</a>), <a href="/wiki/Prince_Henry,_Duke_of_Gloucester" title="Prince Henry, Duke of Gloucester">Prince Henry, Duke of Gloucester</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Prince_George,_Duke_of_Kent" title="Prince George, Duke of Kent">Prince George, Duke of Kent</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Descendants_of_Elizabeth_II">Descendants of Elizabeth II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Windsor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Descendants of Elizabeth II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1947, Princess Elizabeth (now Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a>), heir presumptive to King <a href="/wiki/George_VI" title="George VI">George VI</a>, married <a href="/wiki/Philip_Mountbatten" class="mw-redirect" title="Philip Mountbatten">Philip Mountbatten</a> (born Prince Philip of Greece and Denmark), a member of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Schleswig-Holstein-Sonderburg-Gl%C3%BCcksburg" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Schleswig-Holstein-Sonderburg-Glücksburg">House of Schleswig-Holstein-Sonderburg-Glücksburg</a>, a branch of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Oldenburg" title="House of Oldenburg">House of Oldenburg</a>. A few months before his marriage, Philip abandoned his princely titles and adopted the surname <i><a href="/wiki/Mountbatten" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountbatten">Mountbatten</a></i>, which was that of his uncle and mentor, <a href="/wiki/Louis_Mountbatten,_1st_Earl_Mountbatten_of_Burma" title="Louis Mountbatten, 1st Earl Mountbatten of Burma">the Earl Mountbatten of Burma</a>, and had itself been adopted by Lord Mountbatten's father (Philip's maternal grandfather), <a href="/wiki/Prince_Louis_of_Battenberg" title="Prince Louis of Battenberg">Prince Louis of Battenberg</a>, in 1917. It is the literal translation of the German <i><a href="/wiki/Battenberg_family" title="Battenberg family">Battenberg</a></i>, which refers to <a href="/wiki/Battenberg,_Hesse" class="mw-redirect" title="Battenberg, Hesse">Battenberg</a>, a small town in <a href="/wiki/Hesse" title="Hesse">Hesse</a>.
</p><p>Soon after Elizabeth became Queen in 1952, Lord Mountbatten observed that because it was the standard practice for the wife in a marriage to adopt her husband's surname, the royal house had become the <i>House of Mountbatten</i>. When Elizabeth's grandmother, <a href="/wiki/Mary_of_Teck" title="Mary of Teck">Queen Mary</a>, heard of this comment, she informed British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> and he later advised the Queen to issue a royal proclamation declaring that the royal house was to remain known as the House of Windsor.
This she did on 9 April 1952, officially declaring it her "Will and Pleasure that I and My children shall be styled and known as the House and Family of Windsor, and that My descendants, other than female descendants who marry and their descendants, shall bear the name of Windsor."<sup id="cite_ref-sixty_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sixty-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Philip privately complained, "I am nothing but a bloody amoeba. I am the only man in the country not allowed to give his name to his own children."<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 8 February 1960, some years after both the death of Queen Mary and the resignation of Churchill, the Queen confirmed that she and her children would continue to be known as the "House and Family of Windsor", as would any <a href="/wiki/Agnatic" class="mw-redirect" title="Agnatic">agnatic</a> descendants who enjoy the <a href="/wiki/Style_(manner_of_address)" title="Style (manner of address)">style</a> of <a href="/wiki/Royal_Highness" title="Royal Highness">Royal Highness</a> and the title of prince or princess.<sup id="cite_ref-sixty_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sixty-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Still, Elizabeth also decreed that her agnatic descendants who do not have that style and title would bear the surname <a href="/wiki/Mountbatten-Windsor" title="Mountbatten-Windsor">Mountbatten-Windsor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sixty_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sixty-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>This came after some months of correspondence between the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Harold_Macmillan" title="Harold Macmillan">Harold Macmillan</a> and the constitutional expert <a href="/wiki/Edward_Iwi" title="Edward Iwi">Edward Iwi</a>. Iwi had raised the prospect that the royal child due to be born in February 1960 would bear "the Badge of Bastardy" if it were given its mother's maiden name (Windsor) rather than its father's name (Mountbatten). Macmillan had attempted to rebuff Iwi, until the Queen advised the acting Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Rab_Butler" title="Rab Butler">Rab Butler</a> in January 1960 that for some time she had had her heart set on a change that would recognise the name Mountbatten. She clearly wished to make this change before the birth of her child.  The issue did not affect Prince Charles or Princess Anne, as they had been born with the name Mountbatten, before the Queen's accession to the throne.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Prince_Andrew,_Duke_of_York" title="Prince Andrew, Duke of York">Prince Andrew</a> was born 11 days later, on 19 February 1960.
</p><p>Any future monarch can change the dynastic name through a similar royal proclamation, as royal proclamations do not have statutory authority.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sovereign_states_reigned_over">Sovereign states reigned over</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Windsor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Sovereign states reigned over">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=House_of_Windsor&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">May 2019</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>At the creation of the House of Windsor, its head reigned over the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>. Following the end of the First World War, however, shifts took place that saw the emergence of the <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">Dominions</a> of the <a href="/wiki/British_Commonwealth" class="mw-redirect" title="British Commonwealth">British Commonwealth</a> as independent <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign states</a>. The shift was recognised in the <a href="/wiki/Balfour_Declaration_of_1926" title="Balfour Declaration of 1926">Balfour Declaration of 1926</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_and_Parliamentary_Titles_Act_1927" title="Royal and Parliamentary Titles Act 1927">Royal and Parliamentary Titles Act 1927</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Westminster_1931" title="Statute of Westminster 1931">Statute of Westminster 1931</a>. The Windsors became recognised as the royal family of multiple independent countries, a number that shifted over the decades, as some Dominions became republics and Crown colonies became realms, republics, or monarchies under a different sovereign. Since 1949, two monarchs of the House of Windsor, <a href="/wiki/George_VI" title="George VI">George VI</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a>, have also been <a href="/wiki/Head_of_the_Commonwealth" title="Head of the Commonwealth">Head</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, comprising most (but not all) parts of the former British Empire and some states that were never part of it.
</p>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #addfad; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Current</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Windsor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/British_prince" title="British prince">British prince</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/British_princess" title="British princess">British princess</a></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Windsor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl><dt>Footnotes</dt></dl>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/House_of_Saxe-Coburg_and_Gotha" title="House of Saxe-Coburg and Gotha">House of Saxe-Coburg and Gotha</a> from 6 May 1910 to 17 July 1917; House of Windsor from 17 July 1917 to 20 January 1936.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">After <a href="/wiki/Edward_VIII_abdication_crisis" title="Edward VIII abdication crisis">his abdication in 1936</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edward_VIII" title="Edward VIII">King Edward VIII</a> became <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Windsor" title="Duke of Windsor">the Duke of Windsor</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 1936, virtually all of the functions of the monarch in the Irish Free State were removed, although the monarch was empowered to sign treaties and accredit diplomats when authorised to do so (see <a href="/wiki/Executive_Authority_(External_Relations)_Act_1936" title="Executive Authority (External Relations) Act 1936">Executive Authority (External Relations) Act 1936</a>). In 1937, a new constitution created the office of <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ireland" title="President of Ireland">President of Ireland</a> to perform many of the functions of a head of state. In 1949, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_Act_1948" title="Republic of Ireland Act 1948">Republic of Ireland Act 1948</a> unambiguously severed links with the monarchy. In 1952, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> was the first head of the House of Windsor who did not refer to Ireland (but instead to just <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>) in her regal style.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
